			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">A. P. J. Abdul Kalam</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">

				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">This article is about the former President of India. For the Indian freedom fighter, see <a href="/wiki/Abul_Kalam_Azad" title="Abul Kalam Azad">Abul Kalam Azad</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">In this <a href="/wiki/Indian_name" title="Indian name">Indian name</a>, the name <i>Avul Pakir Jainulabdeen</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Patronymic" title="Patronymic">patronymic</a>, not a <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">family name</a>, and the person should be referred to by the <a href="/wiki/Given_name" title="Given name">given name</a>, <i>Abdul Kalam</i>.</div>

<p><b>Avul Pakir Jainulabdeen Abdul Kalam</b> better known as <b>A.P.J. Abdul Kalam</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/48/En-us-A.p.j._Abdul_Kalam_from_India_pronunciation_%28Voice_of_America%29.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span class="IPA" style="color:#00e;font:bold 80% sans-serif;padding:0 .1em"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-A.p.j._Abdul_Kalam_from_India_pronunciation_(Voice_of_America).ogg" title="File:En-us-A.p.j. Abdul Kalam from India pronunciation (Voice of America).ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/'/ primary stress follows">'</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/?/ short 'oo' in 'foot'">?</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/?/ 'a' in 'about'">?</span><span title="/'/ primary stress follows">'</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/??/ 'a' in 'father'">??</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>; (15 October 1931 – 27 July 2015) was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_India" title="List of Presidents of India">11th</a> <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">President of India</a> from 2002 to 2007. A career scientist turned statesman, Kalam was born and raised in <a href="/wiki/Rameswaram" title="Rameswaram">Rameswaram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Nadu" title="Tamil Nadu">Tamil Nadu</a>, and studied physics and aerospace engineering. He spent the next four decades as a scientist and science administrator, mainly at the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Research_and_Development_Organisation" title="Defence Research and Development Organisation">Defence Research and Development Organisation</a> (DRDO) and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">Indian Space Research Organisation</a> (ISRO) and was intimately involved in India's civilian space programme and military <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Guided_Missile_Development_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="Integrated Guided Missile Development Program">missile development efforts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">[1]</a></sup> He thus came to be known as the <i>Missile Man of India</i> for his work on the development of <a href="/wiki/Ballistic_missile" title="Ballistic missile">ballistic missile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Launch_vehicle" title="Launch vehicle">launch vehicle</a> technology.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> He also played a pivotal organisational, technical, and political role in India's <i><a href="/wiki/Pokhran-II" title="Pokhran-II">Pokhran-II</a></i> nuclear tests in 1998, the first since the <a href="/wiki/Smiling_Buddha" title="Smiling Buddha">original nuclear test by India</a> in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kalam was elected as the 11th President of India in 2002 with the support of both the ruling <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a> and the then-opposition <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a>. Widely referred to as the "People's President,"<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> he returned to his civilian life of education, writing and public service after a single term. He was a recipient of several prestigious awards, including the <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Ratna" title="Bharat Ratna">Bharat Ratna</a>, India's highest civilian honour.</p>
<p>While delivering a lecture at the Indian Institute of Management Shillong, Kalam collapsed and died from an apparent cardiac arrest on 27 July 2015, aged 83.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Thousands including national-level dignitaries attended the funeral ceremony held in his hometown of Rameshwaram, where he was buried with <a href="/wiki/21-gun_salute" title="21-gun salute">full state honours</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Island"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Island</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Other_awards_and_honours"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span class="toctext">Other awards and honours</span></a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Books_and_documentaries"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Books and documentaries</span></a></li>

</ul>
</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life_and_education">Early life and education</span></h2>
<p>Avul Pakir Jainulabdeen Abdul Kalam was born on 15 October 1931 to a <a href="/wiki/Tamil_Muslim" title="Tamil Muslim">Tamil Muslim</a> family in the pilgrimage centre of <a href="/wiki/Rameswaram" title="Rameswaram">Rameswaram</a> on <a href="/wiki/Pamban_Island" title="Pamban Island">Pamban Island</a>, then in the <a href="/wiki/Madras_Presidency" title="Madras Presidency">Madras Presidency</a> and now in the <a href="/wiki/States_and_union_territories_of_India" title="States and union territories of India">State</a> of Tamil Nadu. His father Jainulabudeen was a boat owner and <a href="/wiki/Imam" title="Imam">imam</a> of a local mosque;<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">[9]</a></sup> his mother Ashiamma was a housewife.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KalamTiwari1999_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KalamTiwari1999-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Jai2003_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jai2003-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PIB01march12_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIB01march12-13">[13]</a></sup> His father owned a ferry that took <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> pilgrims back and forth between <a href="/wiki/Rameswaram" title="Rameswaram">Rameswaram</a> and the now uninhabited <a href="/wiki/Dhanushkodi" title="Dhanushkodi">Dhanushkodi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Kalam was the youngest of four brothers and one sister in his family.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> His ancestors had been wealthy traders and landowners, with numerous properties and large tracts of land. Their business had involved trading groceries between the mainland and the island and to and from <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a>, as well as ferrying pilgrims between the mainland and Pamban. As a result, the family acquired the title of "Mara Kalam iyakkivar" (wooden boat steerers), which over the years became shortened to "Marakier." With the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Pamban_Bridge" title="Pamban Bridge">Pamban Bridge</a> to the mainland in 1914, however, the businesses failed and the family fortune and properties were lost over time, apart from the ancestral home.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> By his early childhood, Kalam's family had become poor; at an early age, he sold newspapers to supplement his family's income.<sup id="cite_ref-SharmaDas2004_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SharmaDas2004-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SharmaDas2004_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SharmaDas2004-20">[20]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-visit_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visit-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his school years, Kalam had average grades but was described as a bright and hardworking student who had a strong desire to learn. He spent hours on his studies, especially mathematics.<sup id="cite_ref-visit_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visit-21">[21]</a></sup> After completing his education at the Schwartz Higher Secondary School, Ramanathapuram, Kalam went on to attend <a href="/wiki/St._Joseph%27s_College,_Tiruchirappalli" title="St. Joseph's College, Tiruchirappalli">Saint Joseph's College, Tiruchirappalli</a>, then affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Madras" title="University of Madras">University of Madras</a>, from where he graduated in <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">physics</a> in 1954.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> He moved to <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">Madras</a> in 1955 to study aerospace engineering in <a href="/wiki/Madras_Institute_of_Technology" title="Madras Institute of Technology">Madras Institute of Technology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PIB01march12_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIB01march12-13">[13]</a></sup> While Kalam was working on a senior class project, the Dean was dissatisfied with his lack of progress and threatened to revoke his scholarship unless the project was finished within the next three days. Kalam met the deadline, impressing the Dean, who later said to him, "I was putting you under stress and asking you to meet a difficult deadline".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> He narrowly missed achieving his dream of becoming a fighter pilot, as he placed ninth in qualifiers, and only eight positions were available in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">IAF</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_as_a_scientist">Career as a scientist</span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:280px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div style="margin:0px 2em;">
<p>This was my first stage, in which I learnt leadership from three great teachers—Dr <a href="/wiki/Vikram_Sarabhai" title="Vikram Sarabhai">Vikram Sarabhai</a> , Prof <a href="/wiki/Satish_Dhawan" title="Satish Dhawan">Satish Dhawan</a> and Dr <a href="/wiki/Brahm_Prakash" title="Brahm Prakash">Brahm Prakash</a>. This was the time of learning and acquisition of knowledge for me.</p>
</div>
<div style="position: absolute; left: 0px; top: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">“</div>
<div style="position: absolute; right: 0px; bottom: 0px; text-align: left; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; font-size: large; color: gray;">”</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: right;">A P J Abdul Kalam<sup id="cite_ref-nic_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nic-25">[25]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>After graduating from the <a href="/wiki/Madras_Institute_of_Technology" title="Madras Institute of Technology">Madras Institute of Technology</a> in 1960, Kalam joined the <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Development_Establishment" title="Aeronautical Development Establishment">Aeronautical Development Establishment</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Research_and_Development_Organisation" title="Defence Research and Development Organisation">Defence Research and Development Organisation</a> (DRDO) as a scientist. He started his career by designing a small <a href="/wiki/Hovercraft" title="Hovercraft">hovercraft</a>, but remained unconvinced by his choice of a job at DRDO.<sup id="cite_ref-Sumita_Vaid_Dixit_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sumita_Vaid_Dixit-26">[26]</a></sup> Kalam was also part of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Committee_for_Space_Research" title="Indian National Committee for Space Research">INCOSPAR committee</a> working under <a href="/wiki/Vikram_Sarabhai" title="Vikram Sarabhai">Vikram Sarabhai</a>, the renowned space scientist.<sup id="cite_ref-PIB01march12_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PIB01march12-13">[13]</a></sup> In 1969, Kalam was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">Indian Space Research Organisation</a> (ISRO) where he was the project director of India's first Satellite Launch Vehicle (<a href="/wiki/Satellite_Launch_Vehicle" title="Satellite Launch Vehicle">SLV</a>-III) which successfully deployed the <a href="/wiki/Rohini_(satellite)" title="Rohini (satellite)"><i>Rohini</i></a> satellite in near-earth orbit in July 1980; Kalam had first started work on an expandable rocket project independently at DRDO in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-1">[1]</a></sup> In 1969, Kalam received the government's approval and expanded the programme to include more engineers.<sup id="cite_ref-nic_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nic-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg/220px-Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg/330px-Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg/440px-Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="525" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dr_A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_addresses_the_14th_Convocation_ceremony_at_the_Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kalam addresses engineering students at <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Technology_Guwahati" title="Indian Institute of Technology Guwahati">IIT Guwahati</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1963 to 1964, he visited <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Langley_Research_Center" title="Langley Research Center">Langley Research Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Virginia" title="Hampton, Virginia">Hampton, Virginia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Goddard_Space_Flight_Center" title="Goddard Space Flight Center">Goddard Space Flight Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greenbelt,_Maryland" title="Greenbelt, Maryland">Greenbelt, Maryland</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Wallops_Flight_Facility" title="Wallops Flight Facility">Wallops Flight Facility</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KalamTiwari1999_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KalamTiwari1999-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Inc.1989_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Inc.1989-27">[27]</a></sup> Between the 1970s and 1990s, Kalam made an effort to develop the <a href="/wiki/Polar_Satellite_Launch_Vehicle" title="Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle">Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle</a> (PSLV) and SLV-III projects, both of which proved to be successful.</p>
<p>Kalam was invited by <a href="/wiki/Raja_Ramanna" title="Raja Ramanna">Raja Ramanna</a> to witness the country's first nuclear test <a href="/wiki/Smiling_Buddha" title="Smiling Buddha">Smiling Buddha</a> as the representative of <a href="/wiki/Terminal_Ballistics_Research_Laboratory" title="Terminal Ballistics Research Laboratory">TBRL</a>, even though he had not participated in its development. In the 1970s, Kalam also directed two projects, <i><a href="/wiki/Project_Devil" title="Project Devil">Project Devil</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Project_Valiant" title="Project Valiant">Project Valiant</a></i>, which sought to develop ballistic missiles from the technology of the successful SLV programme.<sup id="cite_ref-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies-28">[28]</a></sup> Despite the disapproval of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Council_of_Ministers_of_India" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Council of Ministers of India">Union Cabinet</a>, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi" title="Indira Gandhi">Indira Gandhi</a> allotted secret funds for these aerospace projects through her discretionary powers under Kalam's directorship.<sup id="cite_ref-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies-28">[28]</a></sup> Kalam played an integral role convincing the Union Cabinet to conceal the true nature of these classified aerospace projects.<sup id="cite_ref-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies-28">[28]</a></sup> His research and educational leadership brought him great laurels and prestige in the 1980s, which prompted the government to initiate an advanced missile programme under his directorship.<sup id="cite_ref-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies_28-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-James_Martin_Center_for_Nonproliferation_Studies-28">[28]</a></sup> Kalam and <a href="/wiki/V._S._R._Arunachalam" title="V. S. R. Arunachalam">Dr V S Arunachalam</a>, metallurgist and scientific adviser to the Defence Minister, worked on the suggestion by the then Defence Minister, <a href="/wiki/R._Venkataraman" title="R. Venkataraman">R. Venkataraman</a> on a proposal for simultaneous development of a quiver of missiles instead of taking planned missiles one after another.<sup id="cite_ref-RV_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RV-29">[29]</a></sup> R Venkatraman was instrumental in getting the cabinet approval for allocating <span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>388 crores for the mission, named <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Guided_Missile_Development_Programme" title="Integrated Guided Missile Development Programme">Integrated Guided Missile Development Programme</a> (IGMDP) and appointed Kalam as the chief executive.<sup id="cite_ref-RV_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RV-29">[29]</a></sup> Kalam played a major part in developing many missiles under the mission including <a href="/wiki/Agni_missile" class="mw-redirect" title="Agni missile">Agni</a>, an intermediate range ballistic missile and <a href="/wiki/Prithvi_missile" class="mw-redirect" title="Prithvi missile">Prithvi</a>, the tactical surface-to-surface missile, although the projects have been criticised for mismanagement and cost and time overruns.<sup id="cite_ref-RV_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RV-29">[29]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IGMDP_Criticism_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IGMDP_Criticism-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kalam served as the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Scientific_Adviser" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Scientific Adviser">Chief Scientific Adviser</a> to the Prime Minister and <a href="/wiki/Secretary_to_Government_of_India" title="Secretary to Government of India">Secretary</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Research_and_Development_Organisation" title="Defence Research and Development Organisation">Defence Research and Development Organisation</a> from July 1992 to December 1999. The <i><a href="/wiki/Pokhran-II" title="Pokhran-II">Pokhran-II</a></i> nuclear tests were conducted during this period in which he played an intensive political and technological role. Kalam served as the Chief Project Coordinator, along with <a href="/wiki/Rajagopala_Chidambaram" title="Rajagopala Chidambaram">Rajagopala Chidambaram</a>, during the testing phase.<sup id="cite_ref-KalamTiwari1999_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KalamTiwari1999-11">[11]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Conley2001_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conley2001-31">[31]</a></sup> Media coverage of Kalam during this period made him the country's best known nuclear scientist.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> However, the director of the site test, K Santhanam, said that the <a href="/wiki/Thermonuclear_bomb" class="mw-redirect" title="Thermonuclear bomb">thermonuclear bomb</a> had been a "<a href="/wiki/Fizzle_(nuclear_test)" title="Fizzle (nuclear test)">fizzle</a>" and criticisied Kalam for issuing an incorrect report.<sup id="cite_ref-pok_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pok-33">[33]</a></sup> Both Kalam and Chidambaram dismissed the claims.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998, along with cardiologist <a href="/wiki/Bhupathiraju_Somaraju" title="Bhupathiraju Somaraju">Soma Raju</a>, Kalam developed a low cost <a href="/wiki/Coronary_stent" title="Coronary stent">coronary stent</a>, named the "Kalam-Raju Stent".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In 2012, the duo designed a rugged tablet computer for health care in rural areas, which was named the "Kalam-Raju Tablet".<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency">Presidency</span></h2>
<p>Kalam served as the 11th President of India, succeeding <a href="/wiki/K._R._Narayanan" title="K. R. Narayanan">K. R. Narayanan</a>. He won the <a href="/wiki/Indian_presidential_election,_2002" title="Indian presidential election, 2002">2002 presidential election</a> with an electoral vote of 922,884, surpassing the 107,366 votes won by <a href="/wiki/Lakshmi_Sahgal" title="Lakshmi Sahgal">Lakshmi Sahgal</a>. His term lasted from 25 July 2002 to 25 July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 10 June 2002, the <a href="/wiki/National_Democratic_Alliance_(India)" title="National Democratic Alliance (India)">National Democratic Alliance</a> (NDA) which was in power at the time, expressed that they would nominate Kalam for the post of President,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> and both the <a href="/wiki/Samajwadi_Party" title="Samajwadi Party">Samajwadi Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Congress_Party" title="Nationalist Congress Party">Nationalist Congress Party</a> backed his candidacy.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> After the Samajwadi Party announced its support for Kalam, Narayanan chose not to seek a second term in office, leaving the field clear.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Kalam said of the announcement of his candidature:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I am really overwhelmed. Everywhere both in Internet and in other media, I have been asked for a message. I was thinking what message I can give to the people of the country at this juncture.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>On 18 June, Kalam filed his nomination papers in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Parliament">Indian Parliament</a>, accompanied by Vajpayee and his senior Cabinet colleagues.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Abdul_Kalam_26_January_2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kalam along with <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a> during his presidency</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The polling for the presidential election began on 15 July 2002 in Parliament and the state assemblies, with the media claiming that the election was a one-sided affair and Kalam's victory was a foregone conclusion; the count was held on 18 July.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Kalam became the 11th president of the Republic of India in an easy victory,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> and moved into the <a href="/wiki/Rashtrapati_Bhavan" title="Rashtrapati Bhavan">Rashtrapati Bhavan</a> after he was sworn in on 25 July.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Kalam was the third President of India to have been honoured with a Bharat Ratna, India's highest civilian honour, before becoming the President. <a href="/wiki/Sarvepalli_Radhakrishnan" title="Sarvepalli Radhakrishnan">Dr Sarvepalli Radhakrishnan</a> (1954) and <a href="/wiki/Zakir_Hussain_(politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Zakir Hussain (politician)">Dr Zakir Hussain</a> (1963) were the earlier recipients of Bharat Ratna who later became the President of India.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> He was also the first scientist and the first bachelor to occupy <a href="/wiki/Rashtrapati_Bhawan" class="mw-redirect" title="Rashtrapati Bhawan">Rashtrapati Bhawan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>During his term as president, he was affectionately known as the <i>People's President</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Misra_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Misra-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> saying that signing the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_profit" title="Office of profit">Office of Profit Bill</a> was the toughest decision he had taken during his tenure.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Kalam was criticised for his inaction in deciding the fate of 20 out of the 21 mercy petitions submitted to him during his tenure.<sup id="cite_ref-hang_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hang-57">[57]</a></sup> Article 72 of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_India" title="Constitution of India">Constitution of India</a> empowers the President of India to grant pardons, and suspend or commute the death sentence of convicts on death row.<sup id="cite_ref-hang_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hang-57">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hang1_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hang1-58">[58]</a></sup> Kalam acted on only one mercy plea in his five-year tenure as president, rejecting the plea of rapist Dhananjoy Chatterjee, who was later hanged.<sup id="cite_ref-hang_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hang-57">[57]</a></sup> Perhaps the most notable plea was from <a href="/wiki/Afzal_Guru" title="Afzal Guru">Afzal Guru</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Kashmiri_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Kashmiri people">Kashmiri</a> terrorist who was convicted of conspiracy in the <a href="/wiki/2001_Indian_Parliament_attack" title="2001 Indian Parliament attack">December 2001 attack on the Indian Parliament</a> and was sentenced to death by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_India" title="Supreme Court of India">Supreme Court of India</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-hang1_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hang1-58">[58]</a></sup> While the sentence was scheduled to be carried out on 20 October 2006, the pending action on his mercy plea resulted in him remaining on death row.<sup id="cite_ref-hang1_58-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hang1-58">[58]</a></sup> He also took the controversial decision to impose President's Rule in Bihar in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2003, in an interactive session in <a href="/wiki/Post_Graduate_Institute_of_Medical_Education_and_Research" class="mw-redirect" title="Post Graduate Institute of Medical Education and Research">PGI Chandigarh</a>, Kalam supported the need of <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Civil_Code" class="mw-redirect" title="Uniform Civil Code">Uniform Civil Code</a> in India, keeping in view the population of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the end of his term, on 20 June 2007, Kalam expressed his willingness to consider a second term in office provided there was certainty about his victory in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_presidential_election,_2007" title="Indian presidential election, 2007">2007 presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> However, two days later, he decided not to contest the Presidential election again stating that he wanted to avoid involving <a href="/wiki/Rashtrapati_Bhavan" title="Rashtrapati Bhavan">Rashtrapati Bhavan</a> from any political processes.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> He did not have the support of the left parties, <a href="/wiki/Shiv_Sena" title="Shiv Sena">Shiv Sena</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Progressive_Alliance" title="United Progressive Alliance">UPA constituents</a>, to receive a renewed mandate.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hindu_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hindu-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nearing the expiry of the term of the 12th President <a href="/wiki/Pratibha_Patil" title="Pratibha Patil">Pratibha Patil</a> on 24 July 2012, media reports in April claimed that Kalam was likely to be nominated for his second term.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> After the reports, <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_sites" class="mw-redirect" title="Social networking sites">social networking sites</a> witnessed a number of people supporting his candidature.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The BJP potentially backed his nomination, saying that the party would lend their support if the <a href="/wiki/Trinamool_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinamool Congress">Trinamool Congress</a>, Samajwadi Party and Indian National Congress proposed him for the <a href="/wiki/Indian_presidential_election,_2012" title="Indian presidential election, 2012">2012 presidential election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> A month ahead of the election, <a href="/wiki/Mulayam_Singh_Yadav" title="Mulayam Singh Yadav">Mulayam Singh Yadav</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mamata_Banerjee" title="Mamata Banerjee">Mamata Banerjee</a> also expressed their support for Kalam.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> Days afterwards, Mulayam Singh Yadav backed out, leaving Mamata Banerjee as the solitary supporter.<sup id="cite_ref-TOI_16_June_2012_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TOI_16_June_2012-76">[76]</a></sup> On 18 June 2012, Kalam declined to contest the 2012 presidential poll. He said of his decision not to do so:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Many, many citizens have also expressed the same wish. It only reflects their love and affection for me and the aspiration of the people. I am really overwhelmed by this support. This being their wish, I respect it. I want to thank them for the trust they have in me.<sup id="cite_ref-toirefused_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toirefused-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-presidency">Post-presidency</span></h2>
<p>After leaving office, Kalam became a visiting professor at the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Shillong" title="Indian Institute of Management Shillong">Indian Institute of Management Shillong</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Ahmedabad" title="Indian Institute of Management Ahmedabad">Indian Institute of Management Ahmedabad</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Indore" title="Indian Institute of Management Indore">Indian Institute of Management Indore</a>; an honorary fellow of <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Science,_Bangalore" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Institute of Science, Bangalore">Indian Institute of Science, Bangalore</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/University_Chancellor" class="mw-redirect" title="University Chancellor">chancellor</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Space_Science_and_Technology_Thiruvananthapuram" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Institute of Space Science and Technology Thiruvananthapuram">Indian Institute of Space Science and Technology Thiruvananthapuram</a>; professor of Aerospace Engineering at <a href="/wiki/Anna_University" title="Anna University">Anna University</a>; and an adjunct at many other academic and research institutions across India. He taught information technology at the <a href="/wiki/International_Institute_of_Information_Technology,_Hyderabad" title="International Institute of Information Technology, Hyderabad">International Institute of Information Technology, Hyderabad</a>, and technology at <a href="/wiki/Banaras_Hindu_University" title="Banaras Hindu University">Banaras Hindu University</a> and Anna University.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2012, Kalam launched a programme for the youth of India called the <i>What Can I Give Movement</i>, with a central theme of defeating corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2011, Kalam was criticised by civil groups over his stand on the <a href="/wiki/Koodankulam_Nuclear_Power_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Koodankulam Nuclear Power Plant">Koodankulam Nuclear Power Plant</a>; he supported the establishment of the nuclear power plant and was accused of not speaking with the local people.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> The protesters were hostile to his visit as they perceived to him to be a pro-nuclear scientist and were unimpressed by the assurances provided by him regarding the safety features of the plant.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:APJAbdulKalam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/APJAbdulKalam.jpg/220px-APJAbdulKalam.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/APJAbdulKalam.jpg/330px-APJAbdulKalam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/APJAbdulKalam.jpg/440px-APJAbdulKalam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="1080" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:APJAbdulKalam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Kalam at <a href="/wiki/Bijnor" title="Bijnor">Bijnor</a> a week before his death</div>
</div>
</div>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wikinews-logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" width="40" height="22" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="759" data-file-height="415" /></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a href="https://en.wikinews.org/wiki/Former_Indian_president_APJ_Abdul_Kalam_dies_at_age_83" class="extiw" title="wikinews:Former Indian president APJ Abdul Kalam dies at age 83">Former Indian president APJ Abdul Kalam dies at age 83</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On 27 July 2015, Kalam travelled to <a href="/wiki/Shillong" title="Shillong">Shillong</a> to deliver a lecture on "Creating a Livable Planet Earth" at the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Management_Shillong" title="Indian Institute of Management Shillong">Indian Institute of Management Shillong</a>. While climbing a flight of stairs, he experienced some discomfort, but was able to enter the auditorium after a brief rest.<sup id="cite_ref-property_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-property-84">[84]</a></sup> At around 6:35&#160;p.m. <a href="/wiki/Indian_Standard_Time" title="Indian Standard Time">IST</a>, only five minutes into his lecture, he collapsed.<sup id="cite_ref-IBN_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBN-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> He was rushed to the nearby Bethany Hospital in a critical condition; upon arrival, he lacked a pulse or any other signs of life.<sup id="cite_ref-IBN_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBN-85">[85]</a></sup> Despite being placed in the <a href="/wiki/Intensive_care_unit" title="Intensive care unit">intensive care unit</a>, Kalam was confirmed dead of a sudden <a href="/wiki/Cardiac_arrest" title="Cardiac arrest">cardiac arrest</a> at 7:45 p.m <a href="/wiki/Indian_Standard_Time" title="Indian Standard Time">IST</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IBN_85-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IBN-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AS_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AS-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> His last words, to his aide <a href="/wiki/Srijan_Pal_Singh" title="Srijan Pal Singh">Srijan Pal Singh</a>, were reportedly: "Funny guy! Are you doing well?"<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following his death, Kalam's body was airlifted in an <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force" title="Indian Air Force">Indian Air Force</a> helicopter from Shillong to Guwahati, from where it was flown to New Delhi on the morning of 28 July in an air force C-130J Hercules. The flight landed at Palam Air Base that afternoon and was received by the President, the Prime Minister, Chief Minister of Delhi <a href="/wiki/Arvind_Kejriwal" title="Arvind Kejriwal">Arvind Kejriwal</a>, and the three service chiefs of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces" title="Indian Armed Forces">Indian Armed Forces</a>, who laid wreaths on Kalam's body.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> His body was then placed on a gun carriage draped with the Indian flag and taken to his Delhi residence at 10 Rajaji Marg; there, the public and numerous dignitaries paid homage, including former prime minister <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a>, Congress President <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Gandhi" title="Sonia Gandhi">Sonia Gandhi</a> and Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Rahul_Gandhi" title="Rahul Gandhi">Rahul Gandhi</a>, and Uttar Pradesh Chief Minister <a href="/wiki/Akhilesh_Yadav" title="Akhilesh Yadav">Akhilesh Yadav</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the morning of 29 July, Kalam's body, wrapped in the Indian flag, was taken to Palam Air Base and flown to <a href="/wiki/Madurai" title="Madurai">Madurai</a> in an air force C-130J aircraft, arriving at <a href="/wiki/Madurai_Airport" title="Madurai Airport">Madurai Airport</a> that afternoon. His body was received at the airport by the three service chiefs and national and state dignitaries, including cabinet ministers <a href="/wiki/Manohar_Parrikar" title="Manohar Parrikar">Manohar Parrikar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venkaiah_Naidu" title="Venkaiah Naidu">Venkaiah Naidu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pon_Radhakrishnan" title="Pon Radhakrishnan">Pon Radhakrishnan</a> and the governors of Tamil Nadu and Meghalaya, <a href="/wiki/K_Rosaiah" class="mw-redirect" title="K Rosaiah">K Rosaiah</a> and <a href="/wiki/V._Shanmuganathan" title="V. Shanmuganathan">V. Shanmuganathan</a>. After a brief ceremony, Kalam's body was flown by air force helicopter to the town of <a href="/wiki/Mandapam" title="Mandapam">Mandapam</a>, from where it was taken in an army truck to his hometown of Rameswaram. Upon arriving at Rameswaram, his body was displayed in an open area in front of the local bus station to allow the public to pay their final respects until 8 p.m. that evening.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 July 2015, the former President was laid to rest at <a href="/wiki/Rameswaram" title="Rameswaram">Rameswaram</a>'s Pei Karumbu Ground with full state honours. Over 350,000 people attended the last rites, including the Prime Minister, the governor of Tamil Nadu and the chief ministers of Karnataka, Kerala and Andhra Pradesh.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg/220px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg/330px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg/440px-Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="474" data-file-height="315" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prime_Minister_Narendra_Modi_pays_homage_to_former_President_APJ_Abdul_Kalam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a> lays a wreath at Kalam's body, on arrival at <a href="/wiki/Indian_Air_Force_Museum,_Palam" title="Indian Air Force Museum, Palam">Palam Air Base</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>India reacted to Kalam's death with an outpouring of grief; numerous tributes were paid to the former President across the nation and on social media.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The Government of India declared a seven-day <a href="/wiki/National_day_of_mourning" title="National day of mourning">state mourning</a> period as a mark of respect.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Pranab_Mukherjee" title="Pranab Mukherjee">Pranab Mukherjee</a>, Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Hamid_Ansari" class="mw-redirect" title="Hamid Ansari">Hamid Ansari</a>, Home Minister <a href="/wiki/Rajnath_Singh" title="Rajnath Singh">Rajnath Singh</a>, and other leaders condoled the former President's demise.<sup id="cite_ref-AS_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AS-87">[87]</a></sup> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a> said "[Dr. Kalam's] death is a great loss to the scientific community. He took India to great heights. He showed the way."<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Former Prime Minister Dr Manmohan Singh, who had served as prime minister under Kalam, said, "our country has lost a great human being who made phenomenal contributions to the promotion of self reliance in defence technologies. I worked very closely with Dr. Kalam as prime minister and I greatly benefited from his advice as president of our country. His life and work will be remembered for generations to come."<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ISRO" class="mw-redirect" title="ISRO">ISRO</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/A._S._Kiran_Kumar" title="A. S. Kiran Kumar">A. S. Kiran Kumar</a> called his former colleague "a great personality and a gentleman", while former chairman <a href="/wiki/G._Madhavan_Nair" title="G. Madhavan Nair">G. Madhavan Nair</a> described Kalam as "a global leader" for whom "the downtrodden and poor people were his priority. He always had a passion to convey what is in his mind to the young generation", adding that his death left a vacuum which none could fill.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asian</a> leaders expressed condolences and lauded the late statesman. The Bhutanese government ordered the country's flags to fly at half-staff to mourn Kalam's death, and lit 1000 butter lamps in homage. Bhutanese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tshering_Tobgay" title="Tshering Tobgay">Tshering Tobgay</a> expressed deep sadness, saying Kalam "was a leader greatly admired by all people, especially the youth of India who have referred to him as the people's President".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Hasina" title="Sheikh Hasina">Sheikh Hasina</a> described Kalam as "a rare combination of a great statesman, acclaimed scientist, and a source of inspiration to the young generation of South Asia" and termed his death an "irreparable loss to India and beyond". <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh_Nationalist_Party" title="Bangladesh Nationalist Party">Bangladesh Nationalist Party</a> chief <a href="/wiki/Khaleda_Zia" title="Khaleda Zia">Khaleda Zia</a> said "as a nuclear scientist, he engaged himself in the welfare of the people". <a href="/wiki/Ashraf_Ghani" title="Ashraf Ghani">Ashraf Ghani</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Afghanistan" title="President of Afghanistan">President of Afghanistan</a>, called Kalam "an inspirational figure to millions of people," noting that "we have a lot to learn from his life". Nepalese Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Sushil_Koirala" title="Sushil Koirala">Sushil Koirala</a> recalled Kalam's scientific contributions to India: "Nepal has lost a good friend and I have lost an honoured and ideal personality." The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Pakistan" title="President of Pakistan">President of Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamnoon_Hussain" title="Mamnoon Hussain">Mamnoon Hussain</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Pakistan" title="Prime Minister of Pakistan">Prime Minister of Pakistan</a> <a href="/wiki/Nawaz_Sharif" title="Nawaz Sharif">Nawaz Sharif</a> also expressed their grief and condolences on his death.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Sri_Lanka" title="President of Sri Lanka">President of Sri Lanka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maithripala_Sirisena" title="Maithripala Sirisena">Maithripala Sirisena</a>, also expressed his condolences. "Dr. Kalam was a man of firm conviction and indomitable spirit, and I saw him as an outstanding statesman of the world. His death is an irreparable loss not only to India but to the entire world."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Maldivian President <a href="/wiki/Abdulla_Yameen" title="Abdulla Yameen">Abdulla Yameen</a> and Vice-President Ahmed Adheeb condoled Kalam's death, with Yameen naming him as a close friend of the Maldives who would continue to be an inspiration to Indians and generations of South Asians. Former president <a href="/wiki/Maumoon_Abdul_Gayoom" title="Maumoon Abdul Gayoom">Maumoon Abdul Gayoom</a>, who had made an official visit to India during Kalam's presidency, termed his demise as a great loss to all of humankind.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The Commander-in-Chief of the <a href="/wiki/Myanmar_Armed_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Myanmar Armed Forces">Myanmar Armed Forces</a>, Senior General <a href="/wiki/Min_Aung_Hlaing" title="Min Aung Hlaing">Min Aung Hlaing</a>, expressed condolences on behalf of the Myanmar government.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a> expressed his sadness and offered condolences and prayers, calling Kalam's death "an irreparable loss".<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kathleen_Wynne" title="Kathleen Wynne">Kathleen Wynne</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Ontario" title="Premier of Ontario">Premier of Ontario</a>, which Kalam had visited on numerous occasions, expressed "deepest condolences ... as a respected scientist, he played a critical role in the development of the Indian space programme. As a committed educator, he inspired millions of young people to achieve their very best. And as a devoted leader, he gained support both at home and abroad, becoming known as 'the people's President'. I join our Indo–Canadian families, friends, and neighbours in mourning the passing of this respected leader."<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> United States President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> extended "deepest condolences to the people of India on the passing of former Indian President Dr. APJ Abdul Kalam", and highlighted his achievements as a scientist and as a statesman, notably his role in strengthening <a href="/wiki/US%E2%80%93India_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="US–India relations">US–India relations</a> and increasing space co-operation between the two nations. "Suitably named 'the People's President', Dr. Kalam's humility and dedication to public service served as an inspiration to millions of Indians and admirers around the world."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Russian President <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> expressed sincere condolences and conveyed his sympathy and support "to the near and dear ones of the deceased leader, to the government, and entire people of India". He remarked on Kalam's outstanding "personal contribution to the social, economic, scientific, and technical progress of India and in ensuring its national security," adding that Dr Kalam would be remembered as a "consistent exponent of closer friendly relations between our nations, who has done a lot for cementing mutually beneficial Russian–Indian cooperation."<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Other international leaders—including former Indonesian president <a href="/wiki/Susilo_Bambang_Yudhoyono" title="Susilo Bambang Yudhoyono">Susilo Bambang Yudhoyono</a>, Malaysian Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Najib_Razak" title="Najib Razak">Najib Razak</a>, Singaporean Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Lee_Hsien_Loong" title="Lee Hsien Loong">Lee Hsien Loong</a>, President of the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_bin_Zayed_Al_Nahyan" title="Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan">Sheikh Khalifa bin Zayed Al Nahyan</a>, and Vice-President and Prime Minister of the United Arab Emirates and <a href="/wiki/Emir" title="Emir">emir</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Rashid_Al_Maktoum" title="Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum">Sheikh Mohammed bin Rashid Al Maktoum</a>—also paid tribute to Kalam.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> In a special gesture, <a href="/wiki/Secretary-General_of_the_United_Nations" title="Secretary-General of the United Nations">Secretary-General of the United Nations</a> <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> visited the <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_mission" title="Diplomatic mission">Permanent Mission of India to the UN</a> and signed a condolence book. "The outpouring of grief around the world is a testament of the respect and inspiration he has garnered during and after his presidency. The UN joins the people of India in sending our deepest condolences for this great statesman. May he rest in peace and eternity", Ban wrote in his message.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>Kalam was the youngest of five siblings, the eldest of whom was a sister, Asim Zohra (d. 1997), followed by three elder brothers: Mohammed Muthu Meera Lebbai Maraikayar (b. 1916; aged 99), Mustafa Kamal (d. 1999) and Kasim Mohammed (d. 1995).<sup id="cite_ref-nephew_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nephew-116">[116]</a></sup> He was extremely close to his elder siblings and their extended families throughout his life, and would regularly send small sums of money to his older relations, himself remaining a lifelong bachelor.<sup id="cite_ref-nephew_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nephew-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-integrity_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-integrity-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kalam was noted for his integrity and his simple lifestyle.<sup id="cite_ref-integrity_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-integrity-117">[117]</a></sup> He never owned a television, and was in the habit of rising at 6:30 or 7 a.m and sleeping by 2 a.m.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> His few personal possessions included his books, his <a href="/wiki/Veena" title="Veena">veena</a>, some articles of clothing, a CD player and a laptop; at his death, he left no will, and his possessions went to his eldest brother, who survived him.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 2011 Hindi film <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Kalam" title="I Am Kalam">I Am Kalam</a></i>, Kalam is portrayed as a positive influence on a poor but bright <a href="/wiki/Rajasthani_people" title="Rajasthani people">Rajasthani</a> boy named Chhotu, who renames himself Kalam in honour of his idol.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_and_spiritual_views">Religious and spiritual views</span></h2>
<p>Religion and spirituality were very important to Kalam throughout his life.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In fact, he made his own spiritual journey the subject of his final book, <i><a href="/wiki/Transcendence:_My_Spiritual_Experiences_with_Pramukh_Swamiji" title="Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swamiji">Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swamiji</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span></h3>
<p>A proud and practising <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, daily <a href="/wiki/Namaz" class="mw-redirect" title="Namaz">namaz</a> and fasting during <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a> were integral to Kalam's life.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-126">[126]</a></sup> His father, the <a href="/wiki/Imam" title="Imam">imam</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a> in his hometown of Rameswaram, had strictly instilled these Islamic customs in his children.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">[9]</a></sup> His father had also impressed upon the young Kalam the value of interfaith respect and dialogue. As Kalam recalled: "Every evening, my father A.P. Jainulabdeen, an imam, Pakshi Lakshmana Sastry, the head priest of the Ramanathaswamy Hindu temple, and a church priest used to sit with hot tea and discuss the issues concerning the island."<sup id="cite_ref-:7_123-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> Such early exposure convinced Kalam that the answers to India's multitudinous issues lay in "dialogue and cooperation" among the country's religious, social, and political leaders.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-125">[125]</a></sup> Moreover, since Kalam believed that "respect for other faiths" was one of the key cornerstones of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, he was fond of saying: "For great men, religion is a way of making friends; small people make religion a fighting tool."<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Syncretism">Syncretism</span></h3>
<p>One component of Kalam's widespread popularity among diverse groups in India, and an enduring aspect of his legacy, is the <a href="/wiki/Syncretism" title="Syncretism">syncretism</a> he embodied in appreciating various elements of the many spiritual and cultural traditions of India.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:5_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-129">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:6_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-130">[130]</a></sup> In addition to his faith in the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Koran</a> and Islamic practice, Kalam was well-versed in Hindu traditions; he learnt <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> read the <a href="/wiki/Bhagavad_Gita" title="Bhagavad Gita">Bhagavad Gita</a><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:4_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-134">[134]</a></sup> and he was a vegetarian.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Kalam also enjoyed writing <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a> poetry, playing the <a href="/wiki/Veena" title="Veena">veena</a> (a South Indian string instrument),<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and listening to <a href="/wiki/Carnatic_music" title="Carnatic music">Carnatic devotional music</a> every day.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_126-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-126">[126]</a></sup> In 2002, in one of his early speeches to Parliament after becoming President, he reiterated his desire for a more united India, stating that "[d]uring the last one year I met a number of spiritual leaders of all religions ... [and] I would like to endeavour to work for bringing about unity of minds among the divergent traditions of our country".<sup id="cite_ref-:5_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-129">[129]</a></sup> Describing Kalam as a unifier of diverse traditions, <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Congress</a> leader <a href="/wiki/Shashi_Tharoor" title="Shashi Tharoor">Shashi Tharoor</a> stated, "Kalam was a complete Indian, an embodiment of the eclecticism of India's heritage of diversity".<sup id="cite_ref-:1_126-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-126">[126]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">BJP</a> leader <a href="/wiki/L._K._Advani" title="L. K. Advani">L. K. Advani</a> concurred that Kalam was "the best exemplar of the Idea of India, one who embodied the best of all the cultural and spiritual traditions that signify India's unity in immense diversity. This was most strikingly evident in the second-to-last book he published, presciently titled <i><a href="/wiki/Transcendence:_My_Spiritual_Experiences_with_Pramukh_Swamiji" title="Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swamiji">Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swami</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pramukh_Swami_as_Guru">Pramukh Swami as Guru</span></h3>
<p>Kalam's desire to meet spiritual leaders to help create a more prosperous, spiritual, and unified India was what initially led him to meet <a href="/wiki/Pramukh_Swami_Maharaj" title="Pramukh Swami Maharaj">Pramukh Swami</a>, the Hindu guru of the <a href="/wiki/Bochasanwasi_Shri_Akshar_Purushottam_Swaminarayan_Sanstha" class="mw-redirect" title="Bochasanwasi Shri Akshar Purushottam Swaminarayan Sanstha">BAPS Swaminarayan Sampradaya</a>, who Kalam would come to consider his ultimate spiritual teacher and guru.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_123-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-125">[125]</a></sup> The first of eight meetings between Kalam and Pramukh Swami over a fourteen-year period took place on 30 June 2001 in New Delhi, during which Kalam described being immediately drawn to Pramukh Swami's simplicity and spiritual purity.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-137">[137]</a></sup> Kalam stated that he was inspired by Pramukh Swami throughout their numerous interactions. One such incident occurred the day following the <a href="/wiki/Akshardham_Temple_attack" title="Akshardham Temple attack">terrorist attack on BAPS</a>' <a href="/wiki/Akshardham_(Gandhinagar)" title="Akshardham (Gandhinagar)">Akshardham, Gandhinagar</a> complex in September 2002; Pramukh Swami prayed for, and sprinkled holy water upon, the sites of all of the deceased, including the terrorists, demonstrating the view that all human life is sacred. Kalam recalled being moved by Pramukh Swami's equanimity and compassion, citing this incident as one of his motivations for writing <i><a href="/wiki/Transcendence:_My_Spiritual_Experiences_with_Pramukh_Swamiji" title="Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swamiji">Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swamiji</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> Summarising the effect that Pramukh Swami had on him, Kalam stated that "[Pramukh Swami] has indeed transformed me. He is the ultimate stage of the spiritual ascent in my life ... Pramukh Swamiji has put me in a God-synchronous orbit. No manoeuvres are required any more, as I am placed in my final position in eternity."<sup id="cite_ref-:2_125-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Following Kalam's death a month after his final book was released, co-author Arun Tiwari pointed to this passage as potentially prophetic and premonitory of Kalam's death.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writings">Writings</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg/220px-A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg/330px-A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg/440px-A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2766" data-file-height="2181" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A.P.J_Abdul_Kalam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A P J Abdul Kalam delivering a speech</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In his book <i>India 2020</i>, Kalam strongly advocated an action plan to develop India into a "knowledge superpower" and a <a href="/wiki/Developed_nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Developed nation">developed nation</a> by the year 2020. He regarded his work on India's <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapons" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuclear weapons">nuclear weapons</a> programme as a way to assert India's place as a future superpower.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>I have identified five areas where India has a core competence for integrated action: (1) agriculture and food processing; (2) education and healthcare; (3) information and communication technology; (4) infrastructure, reliable and quality electric power, surface transport and infrastructure for all parts of the country; and (5) self-reliance in critical technologies. These five areas are closely inter-related and if advanced in a coordinated way, will lead to food, economic and national security.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Kalam describes a "transformative moment" in his life when he asked <a href="/wiki/Pramukh_Swami" class="mw-redirect" title="Pramukh Swami">Pramukh Swami</a>, the guru of the <a href="/wiki/Bochasanwasi_Shri_Akshar_Purushottam_Swaminarayan_Sanstha" class="mw-redirect" title="Bochasanwasi Shri Akshar Purushottam Swaminarayan Sanstha">BAPS Swaminarayan Sampradaya</a>, how India might realise this five-pronged vision of development. &#160;Pramukh Swami's answer—to add a sixth area developing faith in God and spirituality to overcome the current climate of crime and corruption—became the spiritual vision for the next 15 years Kalam's life, which he describes in his final book, <i><a href="/wiki/Transcendence:_My_Spiritual_Experiences_with_Pramukh_Swamiji" title="Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swamiji">Transcendence: My Spiritual Experiences with Pramukh Swamiji</a>,</i> published just a month before his death.<sup id="cite_ref-:8_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was reported that there was considerable demand in South Korea for translated versions of books authored by him.<sup id="cite_ref-Southkorea1_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Southkorea1-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kalam took an active interest in other developments in the field of science and technology, including a research programme for developing <a href="/wiki/Implant_(medicine)" title="Implant (medicine)">biomedical implants</a>. He also supported <a href="/wiki/Open_source" class="mw-redirect" title="Open source">open source</a> technology over <a href="/wiki/Proprietary_software" title="Proprietary software">proprietary software</a>, predicting that the use of free software on a large scale would bring the benefits of information technology to more people.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kalam set a target of interacting with 100,000 students during the two years after his resignation from the post of scientific adviser in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-visit_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visit-21">[21]</a></sup> He explained, "I feel comfortable in the company of young people, particularly high school students. Henceforth, I intend to share with them experiences, helping them to ignite their imagination and preparing them to work for a developed India for which the road map is already available." <a href="/w/index.php?title=His_dream_is_to_let_every_student_to_light_up_the_sky_with_victory_using_their_latent_fire_in_the_heart&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="His dream is to let every student to light up the sky with victory using their latent fire in the heart (page does not exist)">His dream is to let every student to light up the sky with victory using their latent fire in the heart</a>. <sup id="cite_ref-visit_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-visit-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span></h2>
<p>Kalam received 7 <a href="/wiki/Doctor_(title)#Honorary_doctorates" title="Doctor (title)">honorary doctorates</a> from 40 universities.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> The Government of India honoured him with the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Bhushan" title="Padma Bhushan">Padma Bhushan</a> in 1981 and the <a href="/wiki/Padma_Vibhushan" title="Padma Vibhushan">Padma Vibhushan</a> in 1990 for his work with ISRO and DRDO and his role as a scientific advisor to the Government.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> In 1997, Kalam received India's highest civilian honour, the <a href="/wiki/Bharat_Ratna" title="Bharat Ratna">Bharat Ratna</a>, for his contribution to the scientific research and modernisation of defence technology in India.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> In 2013, he was the recipient of the <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Society#Awards" title="National Space Society">Von Braun Award</a> from the <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Society" title="National Space Society">National Space Society</a> "to recognize excellence in the management and leadership of a space-related project".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following his death, Kalam received numerous tributes. The Tamil Nadu state government announced that his birthday, 15 October, would be observed across the state as "Youth Renaissance Day;" the state government further instituted the "<a href="/wiki/Dr._A.P.J._Abdul_Kalam_Award" title="Dr. A.P.J. Abdul Kalam Award">Dr. A.P.J. Abdul Kalam Award</a>," constituting an 8-gram gold medal, a certificate and <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">?</span>500,000</span> (US$7,400). The award will be awarded annually on Independence Day, beginning in 2015, to residents of the state with achievements in promoting scientific growth, the humanities or the welfare of students.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>On occasion of his birth day (2015), <a href="/wiki/Central_Board_of_Secondary_Education" title="Central Board of Secondary Education">CBSE</a> has given the topics on his name in the CBSE expression series.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Prime Minister, Mr. Narendra Modi released the commemorative postal stamps on the former President of India, Dr A.P.J. Abdul Kalam, on his 84th birth anniversary celebrations, at DRDO Bhawan, in New Delhi on 15 October 2015.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Educational_and_scientific_institutions">Educational and scientific institutions</span></h3>
<p>Several educational and scientific institutions and other locations were renamed or named in honour of Kalam following his death.</p>
<ul>
<li>An agricultural college at Kishanganj, Bihar, was renamed the "Dr. Kalam Agricultural College, Kishanganj" by the Bihar state government on the day of Kalam's funeral. The state government also announced it would name a proposed science city after Kalam.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh_Technical_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Uttar Pradesh Technical University">Uttar Pradesh Technical University</a> (UPTU) was renamed "A.P.J. Abdul Kalam Technical University" by the Uttar Pradesh state government.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup></li>
<li>A.P.J. Abdul Kalam Memorial Travancore Institute of Digestive Diseases, a new research institute in <a href="/wiki/Kollam" title="Kollam">Kollam</a> city, <a href="/wiki/Kerala" title="Kerala">Kerala</a> attached to the <a href="/wiki/Travancore_Medical_College_Hospital" title="Travancore Medical College Hospital">Travancore Medical College Hospital</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></li>
<li>A new academic complex at Mahatma Gandhi University in Kerala.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></li>
<li>A new science centre and planetarium in Lawspet, Puducherry.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></li>
<li>India and the US have launched the Fulbright-Kalam Climate Fellowship In September 2014. The first call for applicants was announced on Friday 12 March 2016, for the fellowship which will enable up to 6 Indian PhD students and post-doctoral researchers to work with US host institutions for a period of 6–12 months. The fellowship will be operated by the binational US-India Educational Foundation (USIEF) under the Fulbright programme.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kerala_Technological_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Kerala Technological University">Kerala Technological University</a>, headquartered at <a href="/wiki/Thiruvananthapuram" title="Thiruvananthapuram">Thiruvananthapuram</a> where Kalam lived for years, was renamed to <a href="/wiki/A_P_J_Abdul_Kalam_Technological_University" title="A P J Abdul Kalam Technological University">A P J Abdul Kalam Technological University</a> after his death.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Island">Island</span></h3>
<p>Wheeler Island, a national missile test site in <a href="/wiki/Odisha" title="Odisha">Odisha</a>, was renamed <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Kalam_Island" title="Abdul Kalam Island">Abdul Kalam Island</a> in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></p>

<th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="background: #d3d3d3">1981–2000</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
